                                          </mfrac>
                                       </mfenced>
                                       <mn>2</mn>
                                    </msup>
                                    <msup>
                                       <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                                          <mfrac>
                                             <mrow>
                                                <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                                <msub>
                                                   <mi>E</mi>
                                                   <mi>s</mi>
                                                </msub>
                                             </mrow>
                                             <mrow>
                                                <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                                <msub>
                                                   <mi>E</mi>
                                                   <mi>τ</mi>
                                                </msub>
                                             </mrow>
                                          </mfrac>
                                       </mfenced>
                                       <mn>2</mn>
                                    </msup>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{{D}_{N{{a}^ + }}} = \frac{4}{{\pi \tau }}{{\left( {\frac{{{{m}_B}{{V}_M}}}{{{{M}_B}A}}} \right)}^2}{{\left( {\frac{{\Delta {{E}_s}}}{{\Delta {{E}_\tau }}}} \right)}^2}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>Where <i>τ</i> is the duration time of the current pulse, <i>m<sub>B</sub></i> is the mass of the active material (g), <i>V<sub>M</sub></i> is the molar volume (cm<sup>3</sup> mol<sup>−1</sup>), <i>M<sub>B</sub></i> is the molecular weight (g mol<sup>−1</sup>), <i>A</i> is the total contact area between electrode and electrolyte (cm<sup>2</sup>), <i>ΔE<sub>τ</sub></i> is the variation of the cell voltage, <i>ΔE</i><sub>s</sub> is related to the change of steady-state voltage for the corresponding step. Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#advs8810-disp-0001" title="Link to equation">1</a>) provides a method for calculating the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup> based on the given parameters.</div>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs8810-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="advs8810-sec-0150-title"> Structural Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The crystalline structures of the samples were investigated by both X-ray and neutron diffraction measurements. The X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns of the powder samples were collected by Bruker D8 Discover diffractometer with Cu Kα radiation at room temperature. The neutron powder diffraction (NPD) experiment was carried out on General Purpose Powder Diffractometer (GPPD), a time-of-flight (TOF) diffractometer at China Spallation Neutron Source (CSNS), Dongguan, China. Then the Fullprof program was used to analyze crystal structure by the Rietveld refinement methods.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs8810-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs8810-bib-0023_R_d28775089e1652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Newsletter">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As for in situ XRD studies at the rate of 0.1C, the experiment was carried out on the same XRD diffractometer combined with an in situ device. In situ XRD tests at 10C charging/1C discharging and 10C charging/10C discharging were performed with Liquid Metal Jet Source (Ga Kɑ: 9.24&nbsp;keV, wavelength: 1.3418&nbsp;Å) at the Institute of Advanced Science Facilities, Shenzhen with Dectris PILATUS 1 M detector in the 2θ range of 10°–50°.</p>
                  
                  <p>The morphology and element distribution of the samples were investigated by a scanning electron microscope (SEM, ZEISS SUPRA 55) with an EDS (OXFORD, X-MaxN TSR).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs8810-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="advs8810-sec-0160-title"> Synchrotron X-Ray Absorption Spectroscopy Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The electrodes were dissembled from the coin cells charged or discharged to different states. With high penetration and low absorption, Synchrotron X-ray precisely reflected bulk sample structure properties, which was beneficial when observing tiny phase changes that were usually invisible in laboratory-scale X-ray diffraction due to poor background noise. Hard X-ray absorption spectroscopy (hXAS) of the samples was conducted at the BL11B beamline of Shanghai Synchrotron Radiation Facility (SSRF), Shanghai, China.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs8810-sec-0170">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="advs8810-sec-0170-title"> TEM and STEM Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The TEM and HRTEM were conducted through a transmission electron microscope (TEM, JEM–3200FS, 300&nbsp;keV) with an EDS (OXFORD, X-MaxN TSR). Additionally, electron microscopy including HAADF imaging, ABF imaging, EDS, and EELS was conducted on a Cs-corrected transmission electron microscope (Titan Cubed Themis Z 60–300&nbsp;kV, Thermo Fisher Scientific) operated at 300&nbsp;kV.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="advs8810-sec-0200-title"> Author Contributions</h2>
         
         <p>M.Y. and Z.C. contributed equally to this work. M.Y., Z.C., T.Y., and Y.X. conceived the idea and designed the experiments. M.Y. and Z. Chen. synthesized all the materials and conducted electrochemical measurements. M.Y., Z.C., Z.H., R.W., and D.Z. carried out the in situ XRD and NPD. T.Y. and M.Y. carried out the SEM, TEM, EELS, and STEM measurements and data analysis. M.Y., Z.C. W.J., and T.Z. performed ex situ synchrotron XAS. M.Y., Z.C., T.Y., and Y.X. wrote the manuscript and all authors edited the manuscript.</p>
